Saturday, 10:45 a.m. – Standards of Standard
--------------------------------------------


*by Nate Price*

 

For those of you who want to get a quick and easy foothold on the layout of Standard, here's a basic primer to get you off and running. For those of you who might be new to **Magic**, we've also included a glossary of terms to help you decode some of the jargon we may slip into.


### Deck Archetypes


Hoof, There It Is: According to Jacob Van Lunen, Hoof is the "newest evolution" in the Standard metagame. At its core, Hoof is a Reanimator deck that uses [Unburial Rites](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Unburial+Rites) to bring a [Craterhoof Behemoth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Craterhoof+Behemoth) back into play. Combined with an army of mana critters, the Behemoth is virtually always lethal the turn he comes into play. In addition to reanimating the Behemoth, the presence of [Somberwald Sage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Somberwald+Sage) allows the Behemoth to be cast in the traditional manner, deftly avoiding cards like [Rest in Peace](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rest+in+Peace) and [Rakdos Charm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rakdos+Charm).


Here's Martin Juza's Grand Prix Bochum winning decklist:

![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Forest)

















 

Peddler: One of the most innovative decks to come out of Grand Prix Bochum was the Peddler brew run by Pro Tour Kobe 2006 winner Jan-Moritz Merkel and Max Pritsch. The creature-heavy deck revolves around the *Avacyn Restored* common [Nightshade Peddler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nightshade+Peddler). When paired with [Olivia Voldaren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Olivia+Voldaren) or [Izzet Staticaster](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Izzet+Staticaster), the latter can be used to completely decimate opposing creatures. Considering the prevalence of one-toughness creatures, including the powerful [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls), these cards are very impressive on their own, let alone being able to kill [Thragtusk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thragtusk), [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel), and [Sublime Archangel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sublime+Archangel) in one shot. The deck also runs numerous other creature-based interactions, such as [Zealous Conscripts](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zealous+Conscripts)/[Falkenrath Aristocrat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Falkenrath+Aristocrat)s and [Evil Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Evil+Twin) as a method of dealing with problematic creatures. [Tracker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tracker)'s Instinct makes the deck incredibly more consistent, allowing it to find the numerous two-card combos, as well as filling the graveyard with lands for their [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman)s.


Here is Max Pritsch's 9-0 Day 1 decklist from Grand Prix Bochum:

4-Color Value Rites: Once upon a time, Conley Woods was one of the most renowned deckbuilders in the world. Constantly showing up at tournaments with a deck of his own design, Woods's strong performances gained him a fair amount of notoriety. Nowadays, he has seemingly hung up his brewer's boots for more of a fine-tuning role, content to simply take an already established, solid deck, and enhancing it to work well within the confines of the current environment.


As such, we were a bit surprised when he showed up to Grand Prix San Antonio with this gem:







#### Conley Woods - 4-Color Value Rites


##### 






![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)





[Decklist](#none)
[Stats](#none)
[Sample Hand](#none)

75 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Blood+Crypt)

















 

Woods's basic idea from this deck came from his desire to simply play the best cards in the format. All of the creatures in the deck are incredibly powerful, and the spells are among the best in Standard as well. Unlike other Rites decks, such as the Hoof deck listed above, [Unburial Rites](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Unburial+Rites) isn't a central card to the deck's strategy. Instead, Woods realized that the sheer power of all of his creatures makes [Unburial Rites](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Unburial+Rites) an absolute monster. Since all of his creatures tend to get some sort of advantage for him, reanimating any of them with Rites was nothing but pure, added value.


This deck plays a great deal like Modern Jund. It's a heavy attrition deck that generates card advantage through virtually all of its cards. One of the other major attractions of the deck is its ability to seamlessly transition between offense and defense. Creatures like [Huntmaster of the Fells](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Huntmaster+of+the+Fells), [Thragtusk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thragtusk), and [Loxodon Smiter](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Loxodon+Smiter) are wonderfull both as attackers and in stemming an opponents aggression. The deck has [Farseek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Farseek) and mana critters to give it the speed needed to compete with BR Zombies, as well as the ability to compete with the mana accrual ability of the slower control decks. This surprising resilience and versatility were integral to Woods's success, as he made it all the way to the Semifinals of Grand Prix San Antonio.


For the remainder of the major players in Standard, Jacob Van Lunen wrote an incredibly detailed Standard Compendium which you can check out here.


### Game Concepts



![Brimstone Volley](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Brimstone+Volley)

Burn: Since most of the spells that are capable of directly dealing damage to a player or creature use fire or lightning imagery, they are collectively known as burn spells, even if they don't actually use fire. Examples of burn common to Standard include [Searing Spear](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Searing+Spear), [Pillar of Flame](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pillar+of+Flame), and [Brimstone Volley](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brimstone+Volley).


Card Advantage: The concept of card advantage has received more discussion over the history of **Magic** than any other topic. In short, the concept of card advantage relates to the equivalences of exchanges in **Magic**. Basically, if one card allows you to draw two cards or destroy two of your opponent's permanents, you are gaining card advantage.


ETB: A shorthand acronym for "enters the battlefield". Creatures with ETB effects, such as [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage), have abilities that trigger upon entering the battlefield, giving a spell in the graveyard flashback in the case of [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage). Other textbook examples with cards in Standard with ETB effects are [Craterhoof Behemoth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Craterhoof+Behemoth) and [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel).


Fetch: Fetch is simply a catchall term used to describe the action of retrieving a card from the library. [Farseek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Farseek) is an example of a card that allows players to "fetch" a land from their deck.


Metagame: The term metagame refers to the state of the current Constructed environment, most frequently speaking of the types of decks that are prominent and popular, as well as individual card choices within those decks. For example, if I told you that the three most popular decks in Standard right now were UW Flash, BR Zombies, and GW, you would have a pretty good idea of the Standard metagame. Since each tournament gives players a chance to react to what they experienced in the previous one, the metagame is constantly changing. Staying on top of and correctly predicting the metagame is one of the most challenging aspects of the professional level of **Magic**.


Mill: A verb derived from the card [Millstone](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Millstone), the act of milling a player is to put cards from a player's library into their graveyard. Since players lose the game when they can't draw a card, milling an opponent's entire library is one of the most frequently used alternate win conditions. In Standard, cards such as [Nephalia Drownyard](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nephalia+Drownyard) and [Jace, Memory Adept](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+Memory+Adept), are the most common instances of mill cards.



![Craterhoof Behemoth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Craterhoof+Behemoth)

"#"-Drop: This terminology is used to describe a permanent of a given converted mana cost. For example, [Knight of Infamy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Infamy), which costs 1B, is a two-drop. [Craterhoof Behemoth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Craterhoof+Behemoth) is an eight-drop. This terminology applies most often to permanents, such as creatures and artifacts, but it can be used to also describe the cost of spells.


Red Zone: The red zone is an allusion to the older play mats used for Feature Matches, which had a large red area between the players. Players would use this area to indicate the spells they were casting and the creatures that were attacking. Nowadays, the phrase "sends them into the red zone" is synonymous for attacking.


Swing/Smash/Battle/Bash: All of these words have at some point in **Magic** history been the preferred method of saying "to attack". Now, they are all interchangeable and frequently used as slang.


The Stack: The stack is the order of spells that have been played during a given priority step. For example, when you play a spell in your main phase, it is said to go on the stack. After that, any spells that are played in response to the first one are said to go on the stack above them. Spells on the stack resolve from the top to the bottom.


Silver Bullet: A reference to the very specific weakness of werewolves, the phrase "silver bullet" in **Magic** refers to a card that exists in a deck, usually only one or two copies, that serves the purpose of providing an advantage against a very specific deck or effect. A good example of a silver bullet is the card [Rest in Peace](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rest+in+Peace), which is good against graveyard decks, and [Thundermaw Hellkite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thundermaw+Hellkite), which is especially effective against [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls).


Mirror Match: A match between two decks of the same archetype. For example, two GW decks playing against each other is called the GW mirror match.

---



Saturday, 12:30 p.m. – Keeping Zombies on Top
---------------------------------------------


*by Nate Price*

 

It's tough to stay on top, especially for a **Magic** deck. Once you hit the big time and get your name up in lights, you think you've made it. You think that people are going to love you and want to be just like you. What you don't realize is that you've made yourself a target.


Every time a deck wins a major tournament, the number of people who are playing the deck simply explodes overnight. After all, if its been good enough to last through eighteen rounds of a Grand Prix, it has to be an incredibly strong deck. Players want to ride that wave of success, so many people turn to the tournament-tested winner for their success. The unfortunate thing about this trend is that it's a recognized trend. People know that it's going to happen because it happens every time. Winning a tournament creates the next big deck. As such, players know that they need to be prepared for it in order to deal with the fact that it's going to be virtually everywhere. You've got to be prepared, and you've got to bring the hate. This is the reason that it's not often that you see a deck repeat as a tournament winner unless it undergoes some transformation itself. It has to adapt to counter those people who are adapting to it.



![Pillar of Flame](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Pillar+of+Flame)

BR Zombies is the most recent big deck in Standard **Magic**. After chewing its way to the top of the tournament at Grand Prix Charleston, the deck managed to win the next North American Grand Prix as well. The surprising thing is how little it changed. Of the 75 cards used by Jon Bolding to win Charleston, Tyler Lytle only changed five of them. But those changes were very important. Knowing that BR Zombies was going to be the deck of the tournament, Lytle decided to move the [Pillar of Flame](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pillar+of+Flame) from the sideboard to the maindeck, going up to four, and he added four [Vampire Nighthawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampire+Nighthawk)s to his sideboard. Pillar is wonderful at removing opposing [Geralf's Messenger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Geralf%27s+Messenger)s and [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler)s, and Nighthawk takes over the races that the BR mirrors inevitably become. It's a tactical decision based on the fact that he knew the big deck.


Well, guess what? Nothing has changed. In fact, after winning two tournaments in a row, it's actually even more likely that people will be gunning for Zombies here in Nagoya. A quick glance around the room reveals a sea of black and red cards, leading me to believe that many players have adopted the old adage: If you can't beat 'em, join 'em. Still, since it's impossible to escape the omnipresent Zombie horde, every deck in the field is gearing to pack as much hate as possible for the deck. In order to survive, BR Zombies has to find a way to adapt itself to the apex of hate it's sure to face here this weekend. It appears that many here have risen to that challenge.


It had been accepted going into San Antonio that playing midrange was an impossibility in a world of [Sphinx's Revelation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sphinx%27s+Revelation)s and [Thragtusk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thragtusk)s. In an ironic twist of fate, the slower control decks sped themselves up to have more midrange presence, while the faster decks added more expensive spells to go over the top of the control decks, resulting in a format that felt a lot more midrange than players wanted to admit. As such, it's no surprise to see the first of the changes that appears to be taking place among some Zombies players this weekend.



![Diregraf Ghoul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Diregraf+Ghoul)

If the control decks are speeding up to try and match the aggro decks, and many of the other aggro decks are slowing down, some players have put the pedal to the floor, getting as aggressive as possible. Cards like [Stromkirk Noble](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stromkirk+Noble) and [Rakdos Cackler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rakdos+Cackler) have joined the regular crew of [Diregraf Ghoul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Diregraf+Ghoul) and [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler) to give this ultra-fast Zombies build an incredible density of one-drops. This allows the deck to swarm in enough early damage that their [Geralf's Messenger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Geralf%27s+Messenger)s, [Falkenrath Aristocrat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Falkenrath+Aristocrat)s, and [Thundermaw Hellkite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thundermaw+Hellkite)s are finishers in the truest sense of the word, often needing no more than two swings to finish things off. It also gives the deck a tremendous amount of fodder to use to keep the Aristocrat alive while it does its work.


In addition, a trick that was once brought into being to deal with [Thragtusk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thragtusk) is seeing much more play because of those Aristocrats, which many Pros believe is the new "Best Card in Standard." Using [Mark of Mutiny](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mark+of+Mutiny) or [Zealous Conscripts](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zealous+Conscripts) to steal a [Thragtusk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thragtusk) before sacrificing it to a [Falkenrath Aristocrat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Falkenrath+Aristocrat) or [Bloodthrone Vampire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodthrone+Vampire) went out of style as a maindeck option some weeks ago, but it has resurfaced, mostly due to its incredible power against [Thundermaw Hellkite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thundermaw+Hellkite) and [Falkenrath Aristocrat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Falkenrath+Aristocrat) as well.


One of the biggest advantages to the Aristocrat is its incredible durability, able to survive virtually every one of the most powerful removal spells in the format, as well as able to fight favorably with [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel). [Threaten](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Threaten)-like effects such as the Conscripts and [Mark of Mutiny](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mark+of+Mutiny) usually result in the opposing player simply sacrificing their own Aristocrat rather than foolishly handing it over. As such, the effectively become some of the best single-target removal spells in the format. Considering the prevalence of Zombies and the fact that Bant Control will always be a deck, many Zombies players have moved this package to the maindeck.


We are also beginning to see many more maindeck updates that provide BR Zombies a bit more game against the biggest deck in the field: itself. In San Antonio, one of the biggest innovations to the Zombies deck was the addition of [Vampire Nighthawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampire+Nighthawk) to the sideboard. An absolute all-star in the mirror match, Nighthawk also provides some much needed lifegain in the matchup against GW Humans as well. Combined with [Knight of Infamy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Infamy), the Nighthawk can absolutely steal games in aggressive matchups. In San Antonio, Champion Tyler Lytle was quoted as saying that the main reason that he won many of his mirror matches was the fact that he had more Nighthawks than his opponents. Here in Nagoya, we're beginning to see these sideboarded Nighthawks make their way into players's maindecks. With the abundance of BR Zombies expected in the field, having a maindeck advantage is incredibly important.



![Thundermaw Hellkite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Thundermaw+Hellkite)

Another card that is just incredibly powerful in aggressive matches like the mirror is [Olivia Voldaren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Olivia+Voldaren). Four a mere four mana, you get a 3/3 flier that is capable of pinging off virtually half of the creatures in GW Humans and BR Zombies, including Aristocrat, and stealing those it can't outright kill. She gets big enough to attack through [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel), [Thundermaw Hellkite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thundermaw+Hellkite), and virtually anything else opponents throw in the way. She's immune to [Victim of Night](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Victim+of+Night), [Ultimate Price](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ultimate+Price), and [Pillar of Flame](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pillar+of+Flame), and often gets large enough to survive a [Searing Spear](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Searing+Spear). She's really, really good right now, and many players are clearing out a little space for her in their maindecks.


Finally, an innocuous little piece of removal is poised to make a big splash in a field full of Zombies: [Tragic Slip](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tragic+Slip). 4/1 flying, haste creature that can gain indestructibility, meet instant-speed -1/-1 for B. [Thundermaw Hellkite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thundermaw+Hellkite)? Sacrifice one of my creatures and trigger morbid to kill it. Not to mention the fact that Slip kills almost all of the early creature in both the BR and GW decks... It's a very well positioned card right now, and it appears that many players are beginning to come around to it.


As the weekend progresses, it will be interesting to see which variations and alterations are the most successful. As it becomes clear who is having the most success, we will get together with those players who read the field correctly and made the proper changes to see why they did what they did in their quest to bring home yet another title for the crushing inevitability of BR Zombies.




---



Saturday, 2:30 p.m. – Tracking the Top Tables Part One: Rounds 1-3
------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Nate Price*

 

Every player tries their hardest to read the writing on the walls and determine what the best deck for a given event is. It's an incredibly daunting task that is as much luck as it is skill. You have to take into account the decks that were successful leading up to the event, what changes you expect them to make, and what changes you expect other decks to make to counter them. You have to decide whether you want to play the most popular deck, beat the most popular deck, or beat the deck that beats that. You have so many things to track that you're really simply trying to cover as much ground as you can.


Coming into each Grand Prix, we on the coverage staff try to put our own analysis hats on and determine what we think the makeup of the field is going to be. Just like the players who prepared for this event, sometimes we are right and sometimes we are wrong. In any case, one of the most useful tools we have to improve these skills is to look at the complexion of the top tables and watch how it changes as the tournament progresses. The best decks will rise to the top and we will see the tables morph from what people did play to what they should have played. We get information about what the field actually looks like, but also what innovations made decks successful. As the percentage of archetypes rise and fall, we also get some insight into which decks perform well against others, outpacing them on their way to the top. Once completed, we have a wealth of information that makes our outlook at future events even more reliable.


Every Round, we will be taking a quick glance at the archetypes being played at the top twnety tables, giving us a sample size of forty decks. Every three rounds, we will post the results of our scouting, provide a graph of the data, and offer a quick observation and analysis. By the end of the day, we should have a much better idea of what it takes to survive in Standard.


Here's the first three rounds:


### Round 1


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpnag12/Chart1.jpg)
### Round 2


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpnag12/Chart2.jpg)
### Round 3


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpnag12/Chart3.jpg)
As you can see, BR Zombies and GW Aggro are incredibly popular decks. The strength of [Cavern of Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cavern+of+Souls), a level of resilience against removal, and a strong aggressive base are perfect for keeping the slower control decks at bay. Players have taken note of the relative weakness of control in Standard over the past couple of weeks, so it isn't very surprising to see that the number of control decks being played is so low.



![Huntmaster of the Fells](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Huntmaster+of+the+Fells)

One of the biggest early positive movers is Naya. Both the standard WRG version and the Naya Black version, which dips into black for [Falkenrath Aristocrat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Falkenrath+Aristocrat) and some sideboard cards, have begun replacing the standard GW Aggro decks in the field. Early speculation places the blame for this squarely at the feet of [Bonfire of the Damned](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bonfire+of+the+Damned) and [Huntmaster of the Fells](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Huntmaster+of+the+Fells). Both of these cards are incredibly powerful in a format filled with aggressive creatures, making them perfect to combat the large number of Zombies and GW Aggro decks present.


Coincident with the rise of Naya is the fall of GW Aggro. Many of the same cards that are used to combat BR Zombies, such as [Pillar of Flame](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pillar+of+Flame) and the aforementioned [Huntmaster of the Fells](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Huntmaster+of+the+Fells), are equally as good against GW Aggro decks. Since more decks, including the BR Zombies decks, are gearing up to take on Zombies, GW Aggro could potentially get caught in the crossfire. It will be interesting to see how this plays out over the course of the day.


Of course, it's really too early to say anything concrete, as there have only been two rounds of culling to shape the field. Next round marks another massive influx of players, as the players coming into this event with three byes finally enter the fray. The tale of the next three rounds should be very interesting, as we finally get to see what some of the best names in the game have brought to counter the Zombie horde. As decks continue to rise and fall, we'll continue painting our ever-changing picture of the field. Where do you think we'll go from here? Make your guess and then check yourself against the results three rounds from now!




---



Saturday, 3:30 p.m. – Going Over the Top
----------------------------------------


*by Steve Sadin*

 

If you play **Magic** regularly, you will inevitably hear players explaining that they are looking for ways to "go over the top" of their opponents. And with good reason.


If you have the ability to regularly go over the top of your foes, then you will win (the majority of) the games that go on for any extended period of time. However, if your deck doesn't have the ability to go over the top in a matchup, then you will need to win quickly or cling to every marginal advantage that you can in order to secure your victories.



![Angel of Serenity](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Angel+of+Serenity)

But what does it take for you to actually "go over the top"?


* You need to survive long enough for your (potentially) gamebreaking spells to matter

The mere fact that a deck has a lot of abstractly powerful cards, or cards that are good in stalemates, doesn't mean that the deck is actually capable of going over the top of anyone.


If you play a "powerful card" that has a minimal impact on the game, then by definition, you haven't accomplished anything significant.


However, if your gamebreaking cards are significantly better (and/or faster) than whatever your opponent is able to throw at you, and you're able to consistently advance the game to the point where you can play them (and have them matter) – then you're going to be in very good shape.


* You need your cards to actually trump your opponent's strategy

If you and your opponent are going one-for-one the whole game, then anything from [Angel of Serenity](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Angel+of+Serenity) to [Zealous Conscripts](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zealous+Conscripts) can provide you with the boost that you need to break out of what might otherwise be a very bad situation.


Provided that they actually matter in the matchup.


To get a better understanding of how to go over the top of your opponents in Standard, let's take a look at some of the more commonly seen options.


### [Thragtusk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thragtusk), and [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel)


Early on in *Return to Ravnica* Standard – there were few combinations as potent as [Thragtusk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thragtusk) plus [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel). When uncontested, this combination will yield you an additional 10 life, a 3/3 token, a ¾ flier, and a 5/3 that will give you another 3/3 token if/when it leaves play. That's pretty tough for any unprepared foe to overcome...


### [Sphinx's Revelation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sphinx%27s+Revelation), [Runechanter's Pike](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Runechanter%27s+Pike), and/or [Angel of Serenity](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Angel+of+Serenity)


While building up an army of creatures is certainly an appealing option, Blue-White control decks are often able to keep key threats such as [Thragtusk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thragtusk), off of the board with counterspells, [Supreme Verdict](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Supreme+Verdict)s, and other answers before ultimately taking over the game with a big Sphinx's [Revelation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Revelation), a Runechanter's Pike with a graveyard full of spells, or an [Angel of Serenity](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Angel+of+Serenity).


### [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) plus [Gavony Township](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gavony+Township) and/or [Silverblade Paladin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Silverblade+Paladin) plus [Rancor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rancor)


You don't have to play expensive spells to go over the top of your foes. Sometimes the most potent options at your disposal require very little investment.



![Gavony Township](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Gavony+Township)

If you build up an army of fliers with [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls), then it won't take you long for you to pump them to gigantic sizes with a single [Gavony Township](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gavony+Township).


And it doesn't matter how many [Thragtusk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thragtusk)s your opponent plays if you have a [Silverblade Paladin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Silverblade+Paladin), a [Rancor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rancor), and even just a couple of other creatures that you can use to double strike and trample over whatever (contextually) meager defenses your opponent puts in your way.


### [Falkenrath Aristocrat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Falkenrath+Aristocrat), and [Thundermaw Hellkite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thundermaw+Hellkite)


While [Thragtusk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thragtusk) once spelled doom for Zombie players –the gigantic flying duo of [Falkenrath Aristocrat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Falkenrath+Aristocrat), and [Thundermaw Hellkite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thundermaw+Hellkite) can turn the 5/3 beast into little more than an inconvenience.


So as long as you know what types of answers your opponents have at their disposal ([Thundermaw Hellkite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thundermaw+Hellkite), for example, could turn out to be a relatively weak option if players begin loading up on cards like [Ultimate Price](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ultimate+Price) and [Selesnya Charm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Selesnya+Charm) that can kill the dragon at instant speed for a mere two mana) – and what types of threats your opponents are trying to close out their games with, you should be able to find some very good cards that you can use to go over the top of your foes...


You just have to look for them.




---



Saturday, 6:15 p.m. – Tracking the Top Tables Part Two: Rounds 4-6
------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Nate Price*

 

With the beginning of Round 4, 133 players who have yet to play a Round this tournament entered the fray. That's a massive influx of new players that could be seated on the top tables, so it's not entirely unexpected if the numbers get shaken up a little bit. Here's where we left off:


### Round 3


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpnag12/Chart3.jpg)
So far, we'd seen the number of GW Aggro decks sharply decline, replaced with Naya variants. Other than that, we saw a continued shuffling of some of the less represented decks, with some falling out of the top tables while new decks continually joined. The one truly consistent thing was the presence of BR Zombies at the top of the standings. Seemingly the most popular deck at Grand Prix Nagoya by a large margin, it is hard to tell if its dominating representation on the top tables is due to its consistency, or just sheer numbers.


With that said, here's how the next three rounds played out:


### Round 4


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpnag12/Chart4.jpg)
### Round 5


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpnag12/Chart5.jpg)
### Round 6


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpnag12/Chart6.jpg)
With the influx of players with three byes, there was a jump in the number of players playing Control and Reanimator strategies. The biggest gain for a control deck was the UWR Control deck running [Bonfire of the Damned](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bonfire+of+the+Damned), [Pillar of Flame](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pillar+of+Flame), and [Thundermaw Hellkite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thundermaw+Hellkite). As things continued, its representation stayed fairly strong, understandable since it seems fairly well-equipped to deal with the aggressive creature decks.


Other than that move, and a bit of a wild fluctuation from GW Aggro, things stayed fairly consistent across the board. Jund, Naya, and Zombies all stayed right about where they were after Round 3. The rest of the slots were willed in with varieties of blue-based control decks, a smattering of aggressive creature strategies, and the occasional green midrange deck. One pattern of note certainly has held up, however. GW Aggro appears to have been absolutely decimated, falling sharply from where we saw it start the day, on par with Zombies, to where it sits now, right in the middle of the pack.


Three more rounds to go here at Grand Prix Nagoya! Have we reached stability? Does this provide a representative look at the decks we'll see playing tomorrow? Keep tweeting your predictions, and we'll see how you did in three more rounds!




---



Round 6 Feature Match – Shuu Komuro (Blue White Red Control) vs. Osamu Fujita (Black Red Zombies)
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Steve Sadin*

 

While they haven't ventured outside of Japan for many tournaments recently, Shuu Komuro, and Osamu Fujita remain two of the most well respected players in Japan. And with good reason.


Osamu Fujita very nearly became the first Japanese Pro Tour Champion, but he ultimately fell a single match short of accomplishing that goal when he lost in the finals of Pro Tour Amsterdam in 2004.


However, Fujita's finish there served to herald in a new era.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpnag12/GPNagoya-R6-Osamu-Fujita.jpg) *Osamu Fujita* 
Masashiro Kuroda won Pro Tour Kobe just a few short months later -- and Shuu Komuro became the second Japanese Pro Tour Champion by winning Pro Tour Nagoya in 2005.


Fujita, and Komuro faded away from the international play not long after their best finishes, but the Japanese **Magic** community has absolutely thrived in the time since.


This weekend, Fujita and Komuro both have the chance to show the newest generation of Japanese players a thing or two – but first, they're going to have to get past one another.



![Geralf's Messenger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Geralf%27s+Messenger)

### Game One


After winning the die roll, Fujita got off to a fast start with a pair of [Diregraf Ghoul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Diregraf+Ghoul)s, and a [Geralf's Messenger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Geralf%27s+Messenger) - while Komuro spent his early turns cycling through his deck with a [Thought Scour](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thought+Scour), and an [Izzet Charm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Izzet+Charm).


That time spent setting up his hand paid dividends for Komuro, as he was able to fight back – using a [Pillar of Flame](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pillar+of+Flame), and an Azorious Charm to reduce his opponent's board down to just a single [Diregraf Ghoul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Diregraf+Ghoul). However, the fact that Komuro spent his early turns without making any plays that had an immediate impact on the board continued to haunt him when a second [Geralf's Messenger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Geralf%27s+Messenger) knocked him down to a mere 6 life.


Komuru was able to kill of the Geralf Messenger by using a [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) to flash back [Pillar of Flame](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pillar+of+Flame) – but a [Searing Spear](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Searing+Spear) took out the [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage), and set up an attack that knocked Komuro down to 4.


After the attack, Fujita re-cast his [Diregraf Ghoul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Diregraf+Ghoul), allowing himself to represent lethal damage.


However, a pair of [Pillar of Flame](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pillar+of+Flame)s, and [Moorland Haunt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Moorland+Haunt) allowed Komuro to completely stabilize the board, but he would still need to tread carefully given his precariously low life total.


A [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler) didn't seem like much in the face of Komuro's [Moorland Haunt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Moorland+Haunt), particularly when Komuro drew and cast a Runechatner's Pike.


But before Komuro could go on the offensive himself, a [Cavern of Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cavern+of+Souls) allowed Fujita to resolve a [Thundermaw Hellkite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thundermaw+Hellkite) that cleared away his opponent's token army, and gave him the first game.


Osamu Fujita 1 – Shuu Komuro 0


### Game Two


Fujita mulliganed twice, and sighed before keeping his five card hand.


Komuro opened with a [Thought Scour](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thought+Scour), and an [Augur of Bolas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Augur+of+Bolas) (which failed to find anything), while Fujita had a turn two [Knight of Infamy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Infamy).


Komuro passed his third turn without a play, but when his opponent attacked with a [Knight of Infamy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Infamy), he was able to block it with a [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) (that also allowed him to flashback his [Thought Scour](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thought+Scour)).


Fujita had a replacement [Knight of Infamy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Infamy) – but that would ultimately turn out to be the last spell that he would play all game as Komuro made short work of him with a pair of [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel)s, and a [Pillar of Flame](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pillar+of+Flame).


Osamu Fujita 1 – Shuu Komuro 1



![Knight of Infamy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Knight+of+Infamy)

### Game Three


Both players mulliganed to start the third game, but they were still able to get off to reasonable starts. Fujita had a [Diregraf Ghoul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Diregraf+Ghoul), and a [Knight of Infamy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Infamy) to give himself some early pressure – while Komuro's first play was an [Augur of Bolas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Augur+of+Bolas) that revealed a [Pillar of Flame](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pillar+of+Flame).


Fujita missed his third land drop and had to content himself by casting a [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler), while Komuro (somewhat predictably) [Pillar of Flame](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pillar+of+Flame)d away the [Knight of Infamy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Infamy). A replacement [Knight of Infamy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Infamy) allowed Fujita to continue attacking past his opponent's [Augur of Bolas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Augur+of+Bolas) knocking Komuro down to 11, but Fujita was still stuck on just two lands – a [Dragonskull Summit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dragonskull+Summit), and a [Cavern of Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cavern+of+Souls) naming Vampire.


After passing his turn with no play, Komuro used a [Searing Spear](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Searing+Spear) to kill off his opponent's [Knight of Infamy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Infamy) at the beginning of his combat step– but Fujita nonetheless attacked with his [Diregraf Ghoul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Diregraf+Ghoul) and his [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler). Komuro blocked the [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler), fell to 9, and allowed Fujita to recast the 2/1 from his graveyard before ultimately casting an end of turn [Izzet Charm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Izzet+Charm) to draw cards.


[Pillar of Flame](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pillar+of+Flame) exiled the [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler), and a [Runechanter's Pike](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Runechanter%27s+Pike) threatened to eventually make Komuro's [Augur of Bolas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Augur+of+Bolas) into a force to be reckoned with.


Fujita finally drew a third land, a [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain), but all that he could do was cast a new [Knight of Infamy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Infamy) – and consequently had to sit and watch as Komuro built up his board with another [Augur of Bolas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Augur+of+Bolas), and a [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) that soon picked up a [Runechanter's Pike](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Runechanter%27s+Pike).


But while Komuro focused most of his attention towards taking his offenses to the air, Fujita was able to set up a couple of attacks on the ground that led to the demise of both of his opponent's Augurs. And when he finally found a second black land, Fujita was able to cast a [Victim of Night](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Victim+of+Night) that killed off his opponent's would-be-lethal [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) in combat.


However, that ultimately proved to be too little too late for Fujita.


Fujita's follow up play of [Olivia Voldaren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Olivia+Voldaren) was quickly exiled by [Oblivion Ring](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oblivion+Ring), and a [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) picked up a [Runechanter's Pike](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Runechanter%27s+Pike), forcing Fujita to chump block with his [Diregraf Ghoul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Diregraf+Ghoul).


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpnag12/GPNagoya-R6-Shuu-Komuro.jpg) *Shuu Komuro* 
A replacement [Olivia Voldaren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Olivia+Voldaren) followed – but with only five lands (and thus unable to activate his Vampire), Fujita again had to chump block.


[Falkenrath Aristocrat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Falkenrath+Aristocrat) met a similarly ignominious fate a turn later. And while Fujita was eventually able to [Ultimate Price](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ultimate+Price) away the gigantic wizard – a [Sphinx's Revelation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sphinx%27s+Revelation) for 4, then another for 5 gave Komuro all the creatures and removal spells that he needed to take the match.


**Shuu Komuro 2 - Osamu Fujita 1**




---



Round 8 Feature Match – Tzu-Ching Kuo vs. Kouhei Niwa
-----------------------------------------------------


*by Nate Price*

 

Tzu-Ching Kuo was the first player of eight to arrive in the spacious, centrally-located Feature Match area. As such, he had his pick of the seats.


"This seat was Yuuya last round," he asked me as he pointed to a chair?


"Yes," I told him.


"Did he win," Kuo asked with a grin?


When I smiled and nodded, Kuo pulled it away from the table and set his gear down.


"I'll sit here," he said.


Kuo's opponent this round is Kouhei Niwa. Niwa had managed a 6-1 record to this point with the deck of the tournament thus far: BR Zombies. He was playing a couple great additions aimed at helping evolve the Zombies deck to win the mirror, including [Vampire Nighthawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampire+Nighthawk) and [Tragic Slip](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tragic+Slip). Kuo, on the other hand, was playing a UWR Flash deck similar to the one piloted by Yuuya Watanabe.


Niwa was first on the board, using a [Cavern of Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cavern+of+Souls) on Zombie to play a first-turn [Diregraf Ghoul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Diregraf+Ghoul). At the end of his turn, Kuo cycled through his deck with a [Thought Scour](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thought+Scour). The [Scour](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scour) put a [Searing Spear](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Searing+Spear) into his graveyard and a card in his hand, and he untapped to add a land to his board. Niwa continued to add Zombies to his board, making a second Ghoul and a [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler) on consecutive turns. When he went to attack with his pair of [Diregraf Ghoul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Diregraf+Ghoul)s, Kuo burned one away with a [Searing Spear](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Searing+Spear).


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpnag12/r8-Niwa.jpg) *Kouhei Niwa* 
Before attacking on his next turn, Niwa tried to play a [Falkenrath Aristocrat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Falkenrath+Aristocrat). Unfortunately for him, Kuo had a [Rewind](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rewind) to counter it. This was the first time I could remember in a long time that a creature was countered in a deck with [Cavern of Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cavern+of+Souls). [Deprive](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deprive)d of his Aristocrat, Niwa simply attacked with his two Zombies. Kuo flashed in a [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel), sticking it right in front of the [Diregraf Ghoul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Diregraf+Ghoul). Kuo was down to 12, but that was a fairly reasonable life total considering he was facing down one of the most aggressive decks in the format.



![Supreme Verdict](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Supreme+Verdict)

On Niwa's next turn, things took a decidedly worse turn for Kuo. A [Thundermaw Hellkite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thundermaw+Hellkite) crashed onto the table, tapping down the [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) and clearing the way for a seven-point attack. Kuo fell to 5. When Niwa made the same attack on the next turn, Kuo went all in, using his Angel to block the Hellkite and casting [Sphinx's Revelation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sphinx%27s+Revelation) for two to negate the damage from the [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler). He appeared to be setting up for a [Supreme Verdict](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Supreme+Verdict), and Niwa smelled it. Rather than add another creature to his side, Niwa simply passed the turn.


On his turn, Kuo went ahead and cast the Verdict that he had telegraphed with his last turn. This cleared the board, leaving him at 5 with a reasonable number of cards in hand. Niwa appeared to be out of gas, simply playing a [Knight of Infamy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Infamy) and passing the turn. When Kuo killed it with [Pillar of Flame](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pillar+of+Flame), Niwa had nothing to follow it up.


Kuo had turned the corner, stabilizing at 5 life, but he wasn't out of the woods yet. Niwa's deck contained many creatures with haste, as well as burn spells capable of putting Kuo down if his life remained where it was. While Niwa didn't find one of those hasty attackers, the [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler) he did find allowed him to cast the other two in his graveyard, filling up his board. Kuo cast a [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) at the end of Niwa's turn, for a bit of defense, before untapping and clearing Niwa's side of the table with a [Mizzium Mortars](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mizzium+Mortars).


Afraid of the possibility of a [Falkenrath Aristocrat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Falkenrath+Aristocrat) or [Hellrider](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hellrider), Kuo kept his Angel at home. It was the only thing standing between Niwa and his last 5 life. Eventually, he found an [Augur of Bolas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Augur+of+Bolas), which found him a [Pillar of Flame](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pillar+of+Flame). When Niwa began to tap mana, it wasn't for an Aristocrat or [Hellrider](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hellrider), it was to cast both. Kuo thought for quite .some time before cycling through an [Azorius Charm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Azorius+Charm), finding the [Dissipate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dissipate) he needed to stop the Aristocrat. Niwa's lone [Cavern of Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cavern+of+Souls) was set to Zombie, not Vampire, and it had come back to bite him twice now.



![Jace, Memory Adept](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Jace%2C+Memory+Adept)

And then, it appeared that it wouldn't get a chance to bit him anymore. After drawing for his turn, Kuo tapped two mana for a [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage). Combined with the other eleven lands he had in play, Kuo turned the [Snap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snap)caster into a [Sphinx's Revelation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sphinx%27s+Revelation) for eight, and turned the game around. Now at 13 and holding a massive number of cards, Kuo appeared to be in complete control. Niwa tried to get back into things by using [Searing Spear](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Searing+Spear) on Kuo's Augur, allowing Niwa to kill the [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) with a [Tragic Slip](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tragic+Slip). This cleared the way for an attack for four.


It was the last attack he would get. Over the next turns, Kuo added [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel), [Augur of Bolas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Augur+of+Bolas), and a [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) that [Searing Spear](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Searing+Spear)ed away the [Hellrider](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hellrider). With [Jace, Memory Adept](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+Memory+Adept), following their arrival, Niwa quickly conceded.


Tzu-Ching Kuo 1 - Kouhei Niwa 0


Kuo had won the first game on the back of counterspells, but the story could have easily been drastically different. [Counterspell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterspell)s have become maligned as of late, owing to the fact that so many decks are packing [Cavern of Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cavern+of+Souls). With Niwa unable to force through his two [Falkenrath Aristocrat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Falkenrath+Aristocrat)s, Kuo was able to avoid an almost certain death. If either one of those Aristocrats had hit the table, it is unlikely that Kuo would have been able to stabilize on five life and turn things around with that massive [Sphinx's Revelation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sphinx%27s+Revelation). All this because Niwa's lone Cavern was set to Zombie rather than Vampire.


Niwa unsurprisingly chose to play for the second game of the match. [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler) was the first recruit on Niwa's side, but it was left without a partner on the next turn. Kuo dropped an [Augur of Bolas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Augur+of+Bolas) into play on his turn, effectively stopping the [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler) cold. Switching gears, Niwa added a [Geralf's Messenger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Geralf%27s+Messenger) to his side. The Messenger immediately hit Kuo down to 16, and it would give Niwa a creature capable of getting through Kuo's defenses. When he made a [Cavern of Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cavern+of+Souls) naming Demon on the following turn, Kuo knew that a [Hellrider](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hellrider) was going to follow right after. Sure enough, the hasty Demon hit play, and Niwa did some quick math to determine whether or not he should attack with [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler). He decided against, and passed the attack to Kuo. Before damage, Kuo used [Azorius Charm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Azorius+Charm) to send the [Hellrider](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hellrider) to the top of Niwa's deck, content to slow him down a step. Still, Kuo dropped to 11 from the attack, and he had an uncounterable [Hellrider](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hellrider) in his future.



![Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Gravecrawler)

Kuo untapped, added a fourth land to his side, and passed the turn. Not wanting to smash his [Hellrider](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hellrider) into a [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel), Niwa wisely left it at home, content to lend his triggers from relative safety. Kuo did flash in an Angel, using it to kill the [Geralf's Messenger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Geralf%27s+Messenger) while his Augur blocked the [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler). Kuo dropped to 7. After combat, Niwa returned his [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler) from the graveyard.


Kuo once again simply played a land and passed the turn. When Niwa attacked, Kuo masterfully dealt with the attackers. First, he flashed in a [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage), giving his [Azorius Charm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Azorius+Charm) flashback. Then, he blocked his Angel on the [Hellrider](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hellrider), [Snap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snap)caster on the Messenger, and Augur on the [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler). With blockers declared, Kuo used his Charm to give his team lifelink, gaining 6 life to 10. Niwa cleaned house after combat, using a [Searing Spear](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Searing+Spear) to finish off the Angel before replaying the [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler) and a [Diregraf Ghoul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Diregraf+Ghoul). Kuo once again simply passed the turn, sitting at higher life, but a more precarious situation.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpnag12/r8-Kuo.jpg) *Tzu-Ching Kuo* 
Niwa attacked again. Kuo flashed in a [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) and lined it up in front of the Ghoul. He also blocked the Augur to the [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler) and used [Azorius Charm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Azorius+Charm) to return the Messenger to the top of Niwa's deck. The attack was a wash. Niwa added a replacement [Diregraf Ghoul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Diregraf+Ghoul) to his team and recast his [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler) yet again. On his turn, Kuo continued his trend of doing nothing but playing lands. Niwa didn't have an incredibly powerful attack coming, and Kuo was content to block with his Augur and fill up with a [Sphinx's Revelation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sphinx%27s+Revelation). He did take a hit from the Messenger that he had sent to the top of Niwa's deck, but he still came out ahead.


He pushed his lead even further by using a freshly drawn [Pillar of Flame](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pillar+of+Flame) to outright remove the [Geralf's Messenger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Geralf%27s+Messenger) from play. When Niwa attacked in on the next turn, a flashed-in [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) reset the [Augur of Bolas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Augur+of+Bolas) and allowed Kuo to kill off Niwa's team. When he untapped and added a [Drogskol Reaver](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Drogskol+Reaver) to his team, Kuo appeared to have it in the bag. Between more removal and a large [Sphinx's Revelation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sphinx%27s+Revelation), Kuo managed to once again stabilize at 5 before coming back to win.


**Tzu-Ching Kuo 2 - Kouhei Niwa 0**




---
